class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#A2.SS2.SSS1\" title=\"In B.2 Evaluation ‚Ä£ Appendix B Training and Evaluation Details\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_title\"><span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_ref\">B.2.1 </span>Performance Analysis of Mixed Training with Math</span></a></li>\n</ol>\n</li>\n<li class=\"ltx_tocentry ltx_tocentry_subsection\"><a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#A2.SS3\" title=\"In Appendix B Training and Evaluation Details\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_title\"><span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_ref\">B.3 </span>Performance Analysis of Mixed Training with Coding</span></a></li>\n</ol>\n</li>\n</ol></nav>\n</nav>\n<div class=\"ltx_page_main\">\n<div class=\"ltx_page_content\">\n<article class=\"ltx_document ltx_authors_1line\">\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"p1\">\n<span class=\"ltx_ERROR undefined\" id=\"p1.1\">\\reportnumber</span>\n</div>\n<div class=\"ltx_abstract\">\n<h6 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_abstract\">Abstract</h6>\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"20.1\">Recent advances such as OpenAI-o1 and DeepSeek R1 have demonstrated the potential of Reinforcement Learning (RL) to enhance reasoning abilities in Large Language Models (LLMs). While open-source replication efforts have primarily focused on mathematical and coding domains, methods and resources for developing general reasoning capabilities remain underexplored. This gap is partly due to the challenge of collecting diverse and verifiable reasoning data suitable for RL.\nWe hypothesize that logical reasoning is critical for developing general reasoning capabilities, as logic forms a fundamental building block of reasoning. In this work, we present <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"20.1.1\">SynLogic</span>, a data synthesis framework and dataset that generates diverse logical reasoning data at scale, encompassing 35 diverse logical reasoning tasks. The <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"20.1.2\">SynLogic</span> approach enables controlled synthesis of data with adjustable difficulty and quantity. Importantly, all examples can be verified by simple rules, making them ideally suited for RL with verifiable rewards.\nIn our experiments, we validate the effectiveness of RL training on the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"20.1.3\">SynLogic</span> dataset based on 7B and 32B models. <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"20.1.4\">SynLogic</span> leads to state-of-the-art logical reasoning performance among open-source datasets, surpassing DeepSeek-R1-Distill-Qwen-32B by 6 points on BBEH. Furthermore, mixing <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"20.1.5\">SynLogic</span> data with mathematical and coding tasks improves the training efficiency of these domains and significantly enhances reasoning generalization. Notably, our mixed training model outperforms DeepSeek-R1-Zero-Qwen-32B across multiple benchmarks.\nThese findings position <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"20.1.6\">SynLogic</span> as a valuable resource for advancing the broader reasoning capabilities of LLMs. We open-source both the data synthesis pipeline and the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"20.1.7\">SynLogic</span> dataset at <a class=\"ltx_ref ltx_url ltx_font_typewriter\" href=\"https://github.com/MiniMax-AI/SynLogic\" title=\"\">https://github.com/MiniMax-AI/SynLogic</a>.</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"ltx_abstract\">\n<h6 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_abstract\">Abstract</h6>\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"21.1\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"21.1.1\" lang=\"en\">Recent advances such as OpenAI-o1 and DeepSeek R1 have demonstrated the potential of Reinforcement Learning (RL) to enhance reasoning abilities in Large Language Models (LLMs). While open-source replication efforts have primarily focused on mathematical and coding domains, methods and resources for developing general reasoning capabilities remain underexplored. This gap is partly due to the challenge of collecting diverse and verifiable reasoning data suitable for RL.\nWe hypothesize that logical reasoning is critical for developing general reasoning capabilities, as logic forms a fundamental building block of reasoning. In this work, we present <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"21.1.1.1\">SynLogic</span>, a data synthesis framework and dataset that generates diverse logical reasoning data at scale, encompassing 35 diverse logical reasoning tasks. The <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"21.1.1.2\">SynLogic</span> approach enables controlled synthesis of data with adjustable difficulty and quantity. Importantly, all examples can be verified by simple rules, making them ideally suited for RL with verifiable rewards.\nIn our experiments, we validate the effectiveness of RL training on the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"21.1.1.3\">SynLogic</span> dataset based on 7B and 32B models. <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"21.1.1.4\">SynLogic</span> leads to state-of-the-art logical reasoning performance among open-source datasets, surpassing DeepSeek-R1-Distill-Qwen-32B by 6 points on BBEH. Furthermore, mixing <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"21.1.1.5\">SynLogic</span> data with mathematical and coding tasks improves the training efficiency of these domains and significantly enhances reasoning generalization. Notably, our mixed training model outperforms DeepSeek-R1-Zero-Qwen-32B across multiple benchmarks.\nThese findings position <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"21.1.1.6\">SynLogic</span> as a valuable resource for advancing the broader reasoning capabilities of LLMs. We open-source both the data synthesis pipeline and the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"21.1.1.7\">SynLogic</span> dataset at <a class=\"ltx_ref ltx_url ltx_font_typewriter\" href=\"https://github.com/MiniMax-AI/SynLogic\" title=\"\">https://github.com/MiniMax-AI/SynLogic</a>.</span></p>\n</div>\n<figure class=\"ltx_figure\" id=\"id1\" lang=\"en\"><img alt=\"[Uncaptioned image]\" class=\"ltx_graphics ltx_img_landscape\" height=\"178\" id=\"id1.g1\" src=\"x1.png\" width=\"830\"/>\n</figure>\n<section class=\"ltx_section\" id=\"S1\" lang=\"en\">\n<h2 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_section\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_section\">1 </span>Introduction</h2>\n<figure class=\"ltx_figure\" id=\"S1.F1\"><img alt=\"Refer to caption\" class=\"ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_landscape\" height=\"301\" id=\"S1.F1.g1\" src=\"x2.png\" width=\"747\"/>\n<figcaption class=\"ltx_caption ltx_centering\"><span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure\">Figure 1: </span>The framework of logic data synthesis. The process begins with the selection of suitable tasks and the identification of key parameters that control task difficulty. Next, logic instances are generated with appropriate difficulty control (e.g., setting the grid size of Sudoku to 7). These instances are subsequently formalized into natural language instructions. Each task is paired with a task-specific verifier to check the correctness of responses. This framework enables the systematic synthesis of high-quality logic data, covering a wide range of difficulty levels and 35 task types.</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S1.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S1.p1.1\">The success of Deepseek R1¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(DeepSeek-AI et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib3\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite> and OpenAI-o1¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Jaech et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib7\" title=\"\">2024</a>)</cite> demonstrates the great potential of post-training in advancing strong reasoning capabilities. These works reveal that the core methodology behind these advancements is reinforcement learning with verifiable rewards (RLVR), inspiring numerous replication efforts focused on RL training. However, most of these works have concentrated on the mathematics and coding domains, primarily because it is straightforward to design binary reward rules in these areas¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Zeng et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib24\" title=\"\">2025b</a>, <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib23\" title=\"\">a</a>; Yu et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib22\" title=\"\">2025</a>; Hu et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib6\" title=\"\">2025</a>; Zhang et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib25\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite>.\nTo foster more general and comprehensive reasoning abilities, it is essential to utilize diverse tasks and examples with verifiable rewards.\nIn this work, we concentrate on logical reasoning as a promising domain for this objective, hypothesizing that logical reasoning serves as a fundamental building block for developing general reasoning skills.\nAlthough prior work has explored RL training in the context of logic tasks¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Xie et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib20\" title=\"\">2025b</a>; Pan et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib14\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite>, these efforts have typically focused on a single task, leaving the potential of broader and more diverse synthetic logic datasets largely underexplored.</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S1.p2\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S1.p2.1\">Synthetic logic data presents distinct advantages and challenges. Its synthetic nature allows for unlimited data generation with controllable difficulty levels, enabling the creation of increasingly challenging samples. Additionally, the intrinsic properties of some logic tasks like Sudoku often require trial and backtracking in the reasoning process, which closely relates to the ‚Äúaha moments‚Äù¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(DeepSeek-AI et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib3\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite> in problem-solving. Therefore, the primary advantages of synthetic logic data for RLVR lie in its scalability and inherent characteristics that align well with complex reasoning processes. The main challenge, however, is the complexity of generating and designing specific rules for different logic tasks, as tasks like Game of 24 and Sudoku each require distinct verifiers.</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S1.p3\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S1.p3.1\">Recent works primarily focus on logic evaluation¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Suzgun et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib18\" title=\"\">2022</a>; Ma et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib13\" title=\"\">2024</a>; Kazemi et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib9\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite>, but lack high-quality accessible logical reasoning training data. In this work, to address the gap in comprehensive logic tasks, we present <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S1.p3.1.1\">SynLogic</span>: a logical reasoning data synthesis framework and a comprehensive synthetic logic dataset containing 35 tasks, including typical logical tasks such as Sudoku, Game of 24, and Cipher. For each task, we develop task-specific generation code paired with a corresponding rule-based verifier, allowing for fine-grained difficulty control through adjustable generation hyperparameters.</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S1.p4\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S1.p4.1\">To validate the effectiveness of reinforcement learning on the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S1.p4.1.1\">SynLogic</span> data, we run RL training on it with the GRPO algorithm¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Shao et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib17\" title=\"\">2024</a>)</cite> and implement binary outcome rewards determined by each task‚Äôs verification rules. By adapting recent GRPO training techniques introduced in DAPO¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Yu et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib22\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite>, we successfully train Qwen2.5 Base models¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Yang et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib21\" title=\"\">2024</a>)</cite> on the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S1.p4.1.2\">SynLogic</span> data in a zero RL training setting, achieving progressively longer COT responses and observing the emergence of reflection behaviors.\nStarting from Qwen2.5-7B-Base and Qwen2.5-32B-Base foundations, our models achieve over 8 absolute percentage points improvement on the logic benchmark KOR-Bench¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Ma et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib13\" title=\"\">2024</a>)</cite> compared to their instruction models. Notably, our 32B model surpasses DeepSeek-R1-Distill-Qwen-32B on BBEH¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Kazemi et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib9\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite> tasks by 5 absolute points, establishing <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S1.p4.1.3\">SynLogic</span> as the state-of-the-art open-source dataset for logical reasoning to date. Additionally, both models demonstrate strong generalization to unseen mathematics domains.</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S1.p5\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S1.p5.1\">Furthermore, we explore mixing the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S1.p5.1.1\">SynLogic</span> data with mathematics or coding data for RL training. Surprisingly, conducting the mixed training on Qwen2.5-7B-Base model¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Yang et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib21\" title=\"\">2024</a>)</cite>, incorporating <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S1.p5.1.2\">SynLogic</span> data improves training efficiency for developing mathematical and coding skills. For mathematics, mixed training maintains similar mathematics performance under the same number of training steps, which consume fewer math training samples.\nSimultaneously, mixed training achieves much higher performance on logic tasks.\nA similar trend is observed when mixing <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S1.p5.1.3\">SynLogic</span> with coding data, further demonstrating the complementary benefits of logical reasoning training. Finally, we conduct large-scale mixed training on the Qwen2.5-32B-Base model to enhance the capability of Zero-RL training. Our mixed training achieves superior performance on multiple benchmarks compared to the DeepSeek-R1-Zero-Qwen-32B model, consistently outperforming or matching it on BBEH¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Kazemi et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib9\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite>, KOR-Bench¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Ma et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib13\" title=\"\">2024</a>)</cite>, LiveCodeBench¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Jain et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib8\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite>, and GPQA-Diamond¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Rein et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib15\" title=\"\">2024</a>)</cite>, validating the generalization benefits provided by the inclusion of logical reasoning data.</p>\n</div>\n</section>\n<section class=\"ltx_section\" id=\"S2\" lang=\"en\">\n<h2 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_section\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_section\">2 </span><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.1.1\">SynLogic</span>: Synthesizing Logical Reasoning Data at Scale</h2>\n<figure class=\"ltx_table\" id=\"S2.T1\">\n<figcaption class=\"ltx_caption\"><span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_table\">Table 1: </span>Comparison of <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.T1.3.1\">SynLogic</span> with existing synthetic logic datasets. <sup class=\"ltx_sup\" id=\"S2.T1.4.2\">*</sup>The number of tasks of KOR-Bench is based on the broader categorization in the paper. ‚ÄúTrainable‚Äù indicates style=\"padding-left:4.0pt;padding-right:4.0pt;\">\n<span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S2.T1.5.6.1.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">BBEH¬†</span><cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S2.T1.5.6.1.2.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">(</span>Kazemi et¬†al.<span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S2.T1.5.6.1.3.2.1.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">, </span><a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib9\" title=\"\">2025</a><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S2.T1.5.6.1.4.3\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">)</span></cite>\n</td>\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_center\" id=\"S2.T1.5.6.2\" style=\"padding-left:4.0pt;padding-right:4.0pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S2.T1.5.6.2.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">23</span></td>\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_center\" id=\"S2.T1.5.6.3\" style=\"padding-left:4.0pt;padding-right:4.0pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S2.T1.5.6.3.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;color:#FF0000;\">‚úó</span></td>\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_center\" id=\"S2.T1.5.6.4\" style=\"padding-left:4.0pt;padding-right:4.0pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S2.T1.5.6.4.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;color:#FF0000;\">‚úó</span></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class=\"ltx_tr\" id=\"S2.T1.5.7\">\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_left ltx_border_bb ltx_border_t\" id=\"S2.T1.5.7.1\" style=\"padding-left:4.0pt;padding-right:4.0pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.T1.5.7.1.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">SynLogic</span></td>\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_center ltx_border_bb ltx_border_t\" id=\"S2.T1.5.7.2\" style=\"padding-left:4.0pt;padding-right:4.0pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S2.T1.5.7.2.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">35</span></td>\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_center ltx_border_bb ltx_border_t\" id=\"S2.T1.5.7.3\" style=\"padding-left:4.0pt;padding-right:4.0pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S2.T1.5.7.3.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;color:#006400;\">‚úì</span></td>\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_center ltx_border_bb ltx_border_t\" id=\"S2.T1.5.7.4\" style=\"padding-left:4.0pt;padding-right:4.0pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S2.T1.5.7.4.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;color:#006400;\">‚úì</span></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</figure>\n<section class=\"ltx_subsection\" id=\"S2.SS1\">\n<h3 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_subsection\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection\">2.1 </span>Background</h3>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.SS1.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.SS1.p1.1\">Logical reasoning has long been a crucial indicator of model intelligence¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(ai2, <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib1\" title=\"\">2019</a>; Suzgun et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib18\" title=\"\">2022</a>)</cite>, valued for both its significance and synthetic accessibility. With the advancement of reasoning capabilities in Large Language Models (LLMs), researchers have developed increasingly challenging benchmarks to evaluate logical reasoning abilities¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Kazemi et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib9\" title=\"\">2025</a>; Ma et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib13\" title=\"\">2024</a>)</cite>. However, as illustrated in Table¬†<a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#S2.T1\" title=\"Tab. 1 ‚Ä£ 2 SynLogic: Synthesizing Logical Reasoning Data at Scale\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_tag\">1</span></a>, existing benchmarks either lack training support or are limited to a small number of tasks. Synthetic logic data serves as an important source of verifiable data and offers straightforward control over task difficulty, presenting the potential for developing scalable stronger models by training on it. Consequently, comprehensive synthetic logic datasets are essential for developing general strong reasoning models¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Seed et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib16\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite>.</p>\n</div>\n</section>\n<section class=\"ltx_subsection\" id=\"S2.SS2\">\n<h3 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_subsection\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection\">2.2 </span>The Data Synthesis Framework</h3>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.SS2.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.SS2.p1.1\">To synthesize large-scale, diverse synthetic data, we develop a comprehensive data synthesis framework encompassing 35 tasks. While the benchmarks in Table¬†<a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#S2.T1\" title=\"Tab. 1 ‚Ä£ 2 SynLogic: Synthesizing Logical Reasoning Data at Scale\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_tag\">1</span></a> include a wide variety of tasks, a significant challenge we faced is that nearly all evaluation benchmarks do not open-source their data generation methods. This hinders us from building training data for these logic tasks directly. Therefore, we develop these tasks independently, building the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.SS2.p1.1.1\">SynLogic</span> framework, illustrated in Figure¬†<a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#S1.F1\" title=\"Fig. 1 ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_tag\">1</span></a>. The framework consists of the following key components:</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.SS2.p2\">\n<ol class=\"ltx_enumerate\" id=\"S2.I1\">\n<li class=\"ltx_item\" id=\"S2.I1.i1\" style=\"list-style-type:none;\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_item\">1.</span>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.I1.i1.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.I1.i1.p1.1\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold\" id=\"S2.I1.i1.p1.1.1\">Task Selection</span>\nWe select a diverse set of logic tasks that require non-trivial reasoning, drawing from two carefully curated categories of data sources: (1) widely recognized puzzle problems from logic communities, such as the game of 24, Sudoku, and cryptarithms. Many of these puzzles have been previously highlighted in works like¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Kurtic et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib10\" title=\"\">2024</a>; Li et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib11\" title=\"\">2024</a>; Ma et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib13\" title=\"\">2024</a>)</cite>. (2) Logic tasks featured in established evaluation benchmarks, including BBH¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Suzgun et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib18\" title=\"\">2022</a>)</cite> and BBEH¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Kazemi et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib9\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite>. Detailed descriptions and sources for all 35 tasks can be found in the Appendix¬†<a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#A1.SS1\" title=\"A.1 Task Composition and Sources ‚Ä£ Appendix A Comprehensive Overview of SynLogic\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_tag\">A.1</span></a>.</p>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class=\"ltx_item\" id=\"S2.I1.i2\" style=\"list-style-type:none;\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_item\">2.</span>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.I1.i2.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.I1.i2.p1.1\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold\" id=\"S2.I1.i2.p1.1.1\">Parameter Identification</span>\nFor each task, we identify key parameters that control difficulty (e.g., grid size in Sudoku, or missing numbers in Math Path). These parameters form the basis for scalable and adjustable difficulty data synthesis.</p>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class=\"ltx_item\" id=\"S2.I1.i3\" style=\"list-style-type:none;\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_item\">3.</span>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.I1.i3.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.I1.i3.p1.1\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold\" id=\"S2.I1.i3.p1.1.1\">Logic Instance Generation</span>\nWe formalize the task-specific rules into code by manually implementing rule-based logic generators for each task. These generators are designed to encode the specific constraints and rules of the logic problems, ensuring that the generated instances adhere to the intended task structure (e.g., enforcing the unique digits rule in Sudoku). This rule-based approach allows us to efficiently produce large quantities of data and to cover a broad spectrum of difficulty levels by adjusting the difficulty related parameters. All generated instances undergo automated checks for correctness and solvability.</p>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class=\"ltx_item\" id=\"S2.I1.i4\" style=\"list-style-type:none;\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_item\">4.</span>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.I1.i4.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.I1.i4.p1.1\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold\" id=\"S2.I1.i4.p1.1.1\">Appropriate Difficulty Control</span>\nTo ensure that the generated data is both challenging and learnable, we carefully adjust difficulty-related parameters during data generation. We use strong reasoning models, DeepSeek R1¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(DeepSeek-AI et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib3\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite> and OpenAI-o3-mini to set an upper bound on difficulty: the highest difficulty parameters for which R1 or o3-mini can solve samples with a pass@10 greater than zero, representing the limit of these models‚Äô solvability. This approach prevents the inclusion of instances that are too difficult.\nSimilarly, we use chat models to determine the lower bound of difficulty: the lowest difficulty parameters for which the models achieve a pass rate between 0 and 0.5.\nThis dual-bound approach ensures that the dataset includes a balanced range of samples, maintaining an appropriate level of complexity and learnability.</p>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class=\"ltx_item\" id=\"S2.I1.i5\" style=\"list-style-type:none;\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_item\">5.</span>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.I1.i5.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.I1.i5.p1.1\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold\" id=\"S2.I1.i5.p1.1.1\">Prompt Formalization</span>\nTo facilitate training and evaluation with LLMs, we convert abstract logic instances into natural language prompts using task-specific prompt templates. This step ensures that each instance is accessible to both humans and language models.</p>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class=\"ltx_item\" id=\"S2.I1.i6\" style=\"list-style-type:none;\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_item\">6.</span>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.I1.i6.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.I1.i6.p1.1\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold\" id=\"S2.I1.i6.p1.1.1\">Verification Suite</span>\nFor every task, we implement a dedicated verifier that can automatically check the correctness of model outputs, supporting both training supervision and automatic evaluation.</p>\n</div>\n</li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.SS2.p3\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.SS2.p3.1\">A key innovation in our approach is the development of customized difficulty control mechanisms for each task type. Unlike existing benchmarks that often provide fixed-difficulty evaluation data, our system allows precise calibration of problem complexity through task-specific parameters, such as grid size in Sudoku. This difficulty-tuning capability enables the creation of different difficulty level data, presenting the potential of progressively challenging training curricula. We overcame significant challenges in implementing these controls, as many evaluation benchmarks do not open-source their data generation methods.\nAt last, most tasks in <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.SS2.p3.1.1\">SynLogic</span> are designed with: (1) a data generation code capable of producing varied instances, (2) a corresponding verification rule for evaluating solution correctness, and (3) configurable difficulty parameters to enable controlled difficulty of generated data. We independently develop and generate data for 33 tasks in our dataset, while only the data of 2 tasks (Zebra Puzzle¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Lin et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib12\" title=\"\">2024</a>)</cite> and ARC-AGI¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Chollet, <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib2\" title=\"\">2019</a>)</cite>) are directly adopted from existing open source resources.</p>\n</div>\n<section class=\"ltx_subsubsection\" id=\"S2.SS2.SSS1\">\n<h4 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection\">2.2.1 </span>Risk of Data Contamination</h4>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.SS2.SSS1.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.SS2.SSS1.p1.1\">Although several tasks overlap between our selected tasks and current benchmarks, such as KOR-Bench and BBEH, the synthetic nature of our data, combined with the large synthesis space, makes the probability of generating data identical to benchmark test samples very low ‚Äì we have verified that there are no identical samples between our generated datasets and the benchmark test sets.</p>\n</div>\n</section>\n</section>\n<section class=\"ltx_subsection\" id=\"S2.SS3\">\n<h3 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_subsection\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection\">2.3 </span>The <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.SS3.1.1\">SynLogic</span> Datasets</h3>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.SS3.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.SS3.p1.1\">We synthesized our dataset with controlled difficulty parameters for each task, carefully balancing challenge and learnability to ensure the success of our subsequent experiments ¬ß<a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#S3\" title=\"3 Reinforcement Learning on SynLogic\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_tag\">3</span></a>. To accommodate different model capacities, we developed two distinct versions of our dataset: <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.SS3.p1.1.1\">SynLogic<span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_upright\" id=\"S2.SS3.p1.1.1.1\">-Hard</span></span> for Qwen2.5-32B training and <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.SS3.p1.1.2\">SynLogic<span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_upright\" id=\"S2.SS3.p1.1.2.1\">-Easy</span></span> for Qwen2.5-7B training. <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.SS3.p1.1.3\">SynLogic</span>-Hard presents more complex challenges with its broader difficulty level for each tasks with difficulty upper bound described in ¬ß¬†<a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#S2.SS2\" title=\"2.2 The Data Synthesis Framework ‚Ä£ 2 SynLogic: Synthesizing Logical Reasoning Data at Scale\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_tag\">2.2</span></a>. For <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.SS3.p1.1.4\">SynLogic</span>-Easy, we systematically lower difficulty parameters across all tasks to create easier versions. Despite these adjustments, eight tasks still remain beyond the learning capacity of the 7B model with zero training accuracy after RL, thus we removed them from this easy version, where the details about the removed tasks are provided in Appendix¬†<a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#A1.SS2\" title=\"A.2 SynLogic-Hard and SynLogic-Easy ‚Ä£ Appendix A Comprehensive Overview of SynLogic\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_tag\">A.2</span></a>.\nFinally, we synthesized 33k <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.SS3.p1.1.5\">SynLogic</span>-Hard samples and 16k <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.SS3.p1.1.6\">SynLogic</span>-Easy samples used in subsequent experiments for training, along with 10 validation samples per task, separately for the Easy and Hard validation splits.</p>\n</div>\n<section class=\"ltx_subsubsection\" id=\"S2.SS3.SSS1\">\n<h4 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection\">2.3.1 </span>Difficulty Analysis</h4>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S2.SS3.SSS1.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S2.SS3.SSS1.p1.1\">To assess the difficulty of the synthetic data, we conduct an evaluation on the validation splits, assessing model performance using both avg@8 (average pass rate with eight attempts) and pass@8 (success within eight attempts) metrics. The results, illustrated in Figure ¬†<a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#S2.F2\" title=\"Fig. 2 ‚Ä£ 2.3.1 Difficulty Analysis ‚Ä£ 2.3 The SynLogic Datasets ‚Ä£ 2 SynLogic: Synthesizing Logical Reasoning Data at Scale\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_tag\">2</span></a>, confirm the appropriate difficulty levels for each model scale, demonstrating that our datasets provide suitable training challenges across different model capacities.</p>\n</div>\n<figure class=\"ltx_figure\" id=\"S2.F2\">\n<div class=\"ltx_flex_figure\">\n<div class=\"ltx_flex_cell ltx_flex_size_2\">\n<figure class=\"ltx_figure ltx_figure_panel ltx_align_center\" id=\"S2.F2.sf1\"><img alt=\"Refer to caption\" class=\"ltx_graphics ltx_img_landscape\" height=\"168\" id=\"S2.F2.sf1.g1\" src=\"x3.png\" width=\"226\"/>\n<figcaption class=\"ltx_caption\"><span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure\">(a) </span>7B models on <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.F2.sf1.2.1\">SynLogic</span>-Easy</figcaption>\n</figure>\n</div>\n<div class=\"ltx_flex_cell ltx_flex_size_2\">\n<figure class=\"ltx_figure ltx_figure_panel ltx_align_center\" id=\"S2.F2.sf2\"><img alt=\"Refer to caption\" class=\"ltx_graphics ltx_img_landscape\" height=\"168\" id=\"S2.F2.sf2.g1\" src=\"x4.png\" width=\"226\"/>\n<figcaption class=\"ltx_caption\"><span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure\">(b) </span>32B models on <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.F2.sf2.2.1\">SynLogic</span>-Hard</figcaption>\n</figure>\n</div>\n</div>\n<figcaption class=\"ltx_caption ltx_centering\"><span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure\">Figure 2: </span>Evaluation of task difficulty across our dataset versions. (a) Shows the performance of 7B-scale models on the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.F2.3.1\">SynLogic</span>-Easy dataset, while (b) demonstrates the performance of 32B-scale models on the more challenging <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S2.F2.4.2\">SynLogic</span>-Hard dataset. Results are measured using avg@8 (average pass rate with eight attempts) and pass@8 (success within eight attempts) metrics, illustrating the appropriate difficulty control for each model scale.</figcaption>\n</figure>\n</section>\n</section>\n</section>\n<section class=\"ltx_section\" id=\"S3\" lang=\"en\">\n<h2 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_section\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_section\">3 </span>Reinforcement Learning on <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.1.1\">SynLogic</span> </h2>\n<figure class=\"ltx_table\" id=\"S3.T2\">\n<figcaption class=\"ltx_caption\"><span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_table\">Table 2: </span>Evaluation accuracy (%) of 7B and 32B models across logic benchmarks (<span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.T2.6.1\">SynLogic</span>-Val, KOR-Bench, BBH, BBEH) and mathematical benchmarks (AIME 2024, MATH 500, AMC 2023). For 7B models, <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.T2.7.2\">SynLogic</span>-Val refers to <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.T2.8.3\">SynLogic</span>-Easy, while for 32B models, it refers to <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.T2.9.4\">SynLogic</span>-Hard as described in ¬ß¬†<a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#S2.SS3\" title=\"2.3 The SynLogic Datasets ‚Ä£ 2 SynLogic: Synthesizing Logical Reasoning Data at Scale\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_tag\">2.3</span></a>. All evaluations were conducted under zero-shot conditions, with <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.T2.10.5\">SynLogic</span>-Val and AIME 2024 reported as avg@8 to reduce variance.</figcaption>\n<br class=\"ltx_break\"/>\n<table class=\"ltx_tabular ltx_centering ltx_align_middle\" id=\"S3.T2.11\">\n<tr class=\"ltx_tr\" id=\"S3.T2.11.1\">\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_left ltx_border_r ltx_border_tt\" id=\"S3.T2.11.1.1\" rowspan=\"2\" style=\"padding:0.9pt 2.8pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold\" id=\"S3.T2.11.1.1.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">Model</span></td>\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_center ltx_border_r ltx_border_tt\" colspan=\"4\" id=\"S3.T2.11.1.2\" style=\"padding:0.9pt 2.8pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold\" id=\"S3.T2.11.1.2.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">Logic Benchmarks</span></td>\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_center ltx_border_tt\" colspan=\"3\" id=\"S3.T2.11.1.3\" style=\"padding:0.9pt ltx_align_center\" id=\"S3.T2.11.2.1\" style=\"padding:0.9pt 2.8pt;\">\n<span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.T2.11.2.1.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">SynLogic</span><span id=\"S3.T2.11.2.3.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">BBH</span></td>\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_center ltx_border_r\" id=\"S3.T2.11.2.4\" style=\"padding:0.9pt 2.8pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S3.T2.11.2.4.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">BBEH</span></td>\n<td class=\"ltx_td ltx_align_center\" id=\"S3.T2.11.2.5\" style=\"padding:0.9pt 2.8pt;\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S3.T2.11.2.5.1\" id=\"S3.T2.11.9.8.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;background-color:#F5F5F5;\">57.5</span></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</figure>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S3.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S3.p1.1\">Reinforcement learning with verifiable rewards (RLVR) has emerged as a highly effective approach for enhancing reasoning capabilities in large language models¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Zeng et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib24\" title=\"\">2025b</a>; Yu et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib22\" title=\"\">2025</a>; Hu et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib6\" title=\"\">2025</a>; Zhang et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib25\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite>. Building on these advances, our experimental framework also focuses on applying reinforcement learning techniques to the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.p1.1.1\">SynLogic</span> dataset, leveraging the verifiable nature of logical reasoning tasks. In this section, we validate the effectiveness of reinforcement learning training on the <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.p1.1.2\">SynLogic</span> dataset using Qwen2.5-7B-Base and Qwen2.5-32B-Base models.</p>\n</div>\n<section class=\"ltx_subsection\" id=\"S3.SS1\">\n<h3 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_subsection\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection\">3.1 </span>Setup Details</h3>\n<section class=\"ltx_subsubsection\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS1\">\n<h4 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection\">3.1.1 </span>Training Template</h4>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS1.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS1.p1.1\">Following the DAPO training prompt¬†<cite class=\"ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep\">(Yu et¬†al., <a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#bib.bib22\" title=\"\">2025</a>)</cite>, we modify and design the training prompt template for logic training as shown in Figure¬†<a class=\"ltx_ref\" href=\"https://arxiv.org/html/2505.19641v3#S3.F3\" title=\"Fig. 3 ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 Training Template ‚Ä£ 3.1 Setup Details ‚Ä£ 3 Reinforcement Learning on SynLogic\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_ref_tag\">3</span></a>:</p>\n</div>\n<figure class=\"ltx_figure\" id=\"S3.F3\"><svg class=\"ltx_picture ltx_centering\" height=\"160.03\" id=\"S3.F3.pic1\" overflow=\"visible\" version=\"1.1\" style=\"width:403.2pt;\">\n<span class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S3.F3.pic1.1.1.1.1.1.1\"><span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_bold ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.F3.pic1.1.1.1.1.1.1.1\">SynLogic<span class=\"ltx_text id=\"S3.F3.pic1.2.2.2.1.1\" style=\"width:403.2pt;\">\n<span class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S3.F3.pic1.2.2.2.1.1.1\"><span class=\"ltx_text\" id=\"S3.F3.pic1.2.2.2.1.1.1.1\" style=\"font-size:90%;\">Solve the following problem step by step. First, think about the reasoning process in the mind and then provide the answer. The reasoning process is enclosed within &lt;think&gt; &lt;/think&gt; and the final answer is enclosed within &lt;answer&gt; &lt;/answer&gt; tags, respectively, i.e., &lt;think&gt; reasoning process here &lt;/think&gt; &lt;answer&gt; answer here&lt;/answer&gt;.\\n\\nSolve the following problem step by step. First, think about the reasoning process in the mind and then provide the answer. The reasoning process is enclosed within &lt;think&gt; &lt;/think&gt; and the final answer is enclosed within &lt;answer&gt; &lt;/answer&gt; tags, respectively, i.e., &lt;think&gt; reasoning process here &lt;/think&gt; &lt;answer&gt; answer here&lt;/answer&gt;.</span></span>\n</span></foreignobject></g></g></svg>\n<figcaption class=\"ltx_caption ltx_centering\"><span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure\">Figure 3: </span>The prompt template used for training models on <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_smallcaps\" id=\"S3.F3.2.1\">SynLogic</span> data.</figcaption>\n</figure>\n</section>\n<section class=\"ltx_subsubsection\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS2\">\n<h4 class=\"ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection\">\n<span class=\"ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection\">3.1.2 </span>Reward Design</h4>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS2.p1\">\n<p class=\"ltx_p\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS2.p1.1\">Our reward function employs a binary scoring mechanism that evaluates both format adherence and answer correctness. Specifically, we assign a reward of 1 only when a model-generated response satisfies two criteria: (1) it correctly follows the designated format by including both <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS2.p1.1.1\">&lt;think&gt;</span> <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS2.p1.1.2\">&lt;/think&gt;</span> and <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS2.p1.1.3\">&lt;answer&gt;</span> <span class=\"ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS2.p1.1.4\">&lt;/answer&gt;</span> tags, and (2) the final answer provided is correct. Responses that either deviate from the required format or contain incorrect answers receive a reward of 0.</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"ltx_para\" id=\"S3.SS1.SSS2.p2\">\n<table class=\"ltx_equation Skip to main content We gratefully acknowledge support from the Simons Foundation, member institutions, and all contributors. Donate > cs > arXiv:2410.23123 Help | Advanced Search All fields Title Author Abstract Comments Journal reference ACM classification MSC classification Report number arXiv identifier DOI ORCID arXiv author ID Help pages Full text Search open search GO open navigation menu quick links Login Help Pages About Computer Science > Computation and Language arXiv:2410.23123 (cs) [Submitted on 30 Oct 2024 (v1), last revised 4 Mar 2025 (this version, v2)] Title:On Memorization of Large Language Models in Logical Reasoning Authors:Chulin Xie, Yangsibo Huang, Chiyuan Zhang, Da Yu, Xinyun Chen, Bill Yuchen Lin, Bo Li, Badih Ghazi, Ravi Kumar View a PDF of the paper titled On Memorization of Large Language Models in Logical Reasoning, by Chulin Xie and 8 other authors View PDF HTML (experimental) Abstract:Large language models (LLMs) achieve good performance on challenging reasoning benchmarks, yet could also make basic reasoning mistakes. This contrasting behavior is puzzling when it comes to understanding the mechanisms behind LLMs' reasoning capabilities. One hypothesis is that the increasingly high and nearly saturated performance on common reasoning benchmarks could be due to the memorization of similar problems. In this paper, we systematically investigate this hypothesis with a quantitative measurement of memorization in reasoning tasks, using a dynamically generated logical reasoning benchmark based on Knights and Knaves (K&K) puzzles. We find that LLMs could interpolate and memorize the training puzzles (achieving near-perfect accuracy) after fine-tuning, yet they struggle with slight variations of these puzzles. On the other hand, we show that while fine-tuning leads to heavy memorization, it also consistently improves generalization performance. Through in-depth analyses with perturbation tests, cross difficulty-level transferability, probing model internals, and fine-tuning with wrong answers, we establish that LLMs develop reasoning skills on K&K puzzles alongside memorization. Finally, our analysis based on a per-sample memorization score sheds light on how LLMs switch between reasoning and memorization when solving logical puzzles. Our code and data are available at this https URL.
